Bradley Heppner (2026)\n\nOn February 17, 2026, the Southern District of New York held that a criminal defendant's exchanges with a \"publicly available AI platform\" are not protected by attorney-client privilege or work product doctrine, marking the first federal decision addressing privilege claims for communications with a generative AI platform.\n\n### The Case Background\n\nJudge Rakoff ruled that documents generated through a public AI platform (specifically Anthropic's Claude) by defendant Bradley Heppner, who was arrested on federal fraud charges, were not protected by attorney-client privilege or work product doctrine.\n\n### Court's Key Findings\n\nThe court rejected privilege claims on three grounds:\n\n1. **No Attorney-Client Relationship**: The AI platform is not a lawyer, and no attorney-client relationship existed between the defendant and the platform.(no content)Judge Rakoff wrote that no attorney-client relationship exists \"or could exist, between an AI user and a platform such as Claude.\"\n\n2. **No Confidentiality**: The AI platform's privacy policy disclosed that it collects user inputs and outputs, uses data to train the model, and may disclose data to third parties, including government authorities.\n\n3. **Not for Legal Advice**: Anthropic's terms disclaim providing legal advice, and when asked directly, Claude responds: \"I'm not a lawyer and can't provide formal legal advice or recommendations.\"\n\n### Privilege Waiver Implications\n\nThe court noted that inputting privileged materials into a consumer AI tool could waive the privilege over the underlying communications themselves, suggesting this aspect may carry the broadest practical implications.\n\n### Legal Industry Response\n\nThe ruling prompted more than a dozen major U.S. law firms to warn clients that their AI exchanges could be used against them in court.(no content)Firms including O'Melveny & Myers suggest that enterprise-grade, closed AI platforms may carry fewer disclosure risks than consumer tools, though the legal landscape around even those systems has yet to be tested in
